When it dissolves, bathe the area with much water and oil, then treat it with the nukli plaster and the basilicon plaster until it heals. If there is a hot swelling or suppuration in the wound, such as blood clotting in the bladder preventing urination, which is known by blood coming out with urine.
Insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will lead to corruption and infection of the bladder. Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt, and treat each type as appropriate until it heals.
It is necessary at all times of treatment to bind the thighs together to keep the medicines in place that are put on the area. If the stone is small and has entered the urethra and become stuck, preventing urine from passing, treat it as I will describe before resorting to incision.
For I have often been able to avoid incision with this treatment, as I have tried it. It involves taking a splinter of steel that looks like this:
Sharpen the tip to a triangle and fix it to a handle. Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it does not return to the bladder. Then gently insert the steel splinter into the urethra until the prong reaches the stone itself.
Rotate the prong with your hand in the stone little by little, aiming to pierce it until you penetrate through the other side. Then the urine will flow immediately. Then grasp what remains of the stone from outside the penis with your hand; it will crumble and come out with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
If this treatment is not possible for you due to an obstacle hindering you, tie a thread under the stone and another thread above the stone, then incise on the stone in the same rod between the two ties, then extract it.
Then untie the ligature and clean the clotted blood that has formed in the wound. The thread must be tied under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder, and the other thread above so that when the thread is untied after the stone's removal, the skin returns to its place, covering the wound.
Therefore, you should, when tying the upper thread, lift the skin upwards so that it returns to its place upon finishing and covers the wound as we have said.
Chapter Sixty-One.
On Removing Stones from Women.
Stones rarely form in women. If one of them does have a stone, treating it is difficult and often impossible for various reasons: one being that the woman may be a virgin, and another being that you may not find a woman who allows herself to be examined by a doctor.
If she is chaste or from those with kinship restrictions, and thirdly, you may not find a woman skilled in this craft, especially manual work. The fourth reason is that the incision site on the stone for women is far from the location of the stone, so it requires a deep incision.
This carries a risk. If necessity calls for it, you should seek out a skilled female doctor, though they are rare. If you cannot find one, seek a chaste and gentle male doctor, or have a skilled midwife present who is knowledgeable about women's affairs, or a woman who has some experience in this craft.
Prepare her and command her to do all that is instructed, such as examining the stone first. This means she should check if the woman is a virgin; it is appropriate for the finger to be inserted into her anus to search for the stone. If found, press it with the finger.
Then command her to part [herself]. If she is not a virgin but married, instruct the midwife to insert her finger into the patient's vagina and search for the stone after placing her left hand on the bladder and squeezing it well.
If she finds it, she should guide it from the mouth of the bladder downward to the extent of her ability until she reaches the base of the thigh. Then, she should make an incision opposite half of the vagina at the base of the thigh on whichever side is accessible and where she feels the stone.
And her finger should not leave the stone, pressing under it. The incision should be small at first, then insert the probe into that small incision. If she feels the stone, increase the size of the incision according to what is known for the stone to come out from. Know that there are many types of stones.
There are small ones and large ones, smooth and rough, long and round, and those with branches. Recognize their types to understand what you need. If the blood overpowers you, sprinkle powdered zadj in the area and hold it for a while until the bleeding stops, then return to your work.
Continue until the stone is removed. Prepare with yourself the instruments mentioned for removing stones from men to assist you in your work. If bleeding overpowers you and you know by the pulsation of the blood that an artery has been cut, apply the cautery to the area.
And bind it tightly with bandages and leave it without revisiting it and leave the stone without extracting it for perhaps the patient may die then treat the wound if the intensity of the blood subsides after days and the area becomes putrefied return to your work until you extract the stone.
Chapter Sixty-Two.
On Incising the Water Bladder.
The water bladder is an accumulation of moisture in the white membrane that lies under the skin surrounding the testicle, which is called the scrotum. It may be contained in a special sac prepared by nature on one side of the testicle.
Until it is thought to be another testicle, and it is between the scrotal skin and the white membrane we mentioned. This does not occur except rarely. This water bladder develops due to a weakness in the testicles, leading this material to accumulate, and it can result from an impact on the testicles.
This moisture can have various colors; it may be yellowish, or reddish like blood, or dark black, or more commonly, clear and white. These are the signs by which it is recognized.
Where the water accumulates, if it is in the white membrane we mentioned, the swelling will be round and slightly elongated like the shape of an egg, and the testicle will not be visible because the moisture surrounds it on all sides.
If the moisture is in a special sac for it, then the swelling will be round on one side of the testicle.
For this reason, a person may imagine that it is another egg. If the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, then it can be sensed. But if you want to know the color of the moisture, press the swelling with the square probe whose image was previously described; judge its contents by what comes out in the probe's trail.
When we come to treatment with iron, it should be that you order the patient to bleed if that is possible for him and you see his body full. Then he lies on his back on something slightly elevated and you place many cloths under him. Then you sit on his left side.
And you command a servant to sit on his right, extending his member toward one side of the scrotum skin and toward the flank of the abdomen. Then you take a wide scalpel and cut the scrotum skin lengthwise from the middle nearly to the groin.
The incision should be straight, parallel to the line that divides the scrotum skin into two halves until it reaches the white membrane containing it. You peel it back and be careful not to cut it. Your peeling should be from the side that adheres more to the testicle, and you extend the peeling as much as you can.
Then you widely suture the water-filled membrane and remove all the water. Then you separate the edges of the incision with forceps and pull the membrane upwards without touching the scrotal skin containing it, and cut the membrane as much as possible, either entirely or in pieces.
Especially the thin side, for if you do not thoroughly cut it, you cannot be sure that the water will not return. If the testicle protrudes outside its skin while you are working, once you finish cutting the membrane, put it back and then suture the edges of the scrotal skin together.
Then treat it as you would other surgeries until it heals. If the egg has rotted due to another illness, it is necessary to tie the vessels in the scrotum to prevent bleeding, then cut the testicle from the scrotum and remove the egg, then treat it as we have mentioned.
If the water collected on both sides, then know that they are kidneys. Incise the other side as you did with the first, equally. If it is possible for the procedure to be the same, do so, then clean the blood.
Insert wool that has been dipped in oil or rose fat into the incisions, and place another piece of wool that has been dipped in a potion and oil on the outside over the testicles and the abdominal discharge, then cover it with folded cloths, which are the bandages. And bind it above with a six-terminal bandage in this manner:.
Then take two cloths, sew and stuff them with loose wool as in this example, make the ends that need to be tightened from cotton or damp wool, gather them by pulling into the waistband, and one end should go around the buttocks to the back.
The second should be taken towards the groin, with the two ends on the thighs below and the remaining two ends on the buttocks, gather all the tension into the waistband. This procedure for the kidneys can also be done by cauterization instead of incision with iron.
This is done by taking a sharp cauterizing iron and incising the skin of the testicle while it is hot, as described, until the white membrane containing the water is exposed. Take another cauterizing iron in this manner:.
It resembles the Greek eye, then apply that wrapping while it is warm until all moisture comes out, then stretch the wrapping with irons and peel the layer containing it with an iron and cut it as much as possible until you completely remove it and be careful of the egg so that fire does not touch it.
And know that this procedure is safer and involves less bloodletting and is better than incision. If you encounter a hot swelling or bleeding or anything else during the incision or cauterization, you should treat each of those complications with the appropriate treatment as previously mentioned.
If the patient is timid and cannot tolerate this procedure due to its severity, then use wrapping as I will describe. This should be validated by you with the evidence we have provided.
The edema is watery, so the patient should sit on a high chair, then wrap the swelling at its base with a wide instrument. Place the wrapping along the length of the body and make the opening wide enough for all the water to drain out, then put cotton on the area and bind it.
Leave it to drain the remaining water, then treat it until the wound heals. If the water does not come out easily while you are wrapping it, it is likely because the white membrane obstructs the mouth of the wound, preventing the water from exiting.
In that case, you should insert a duck feather or the instrument used to extract water from blisters, which was previously described, or slightly enlarge the wound opening.
Know that the water may return and collect after about six months. If it collects, wrap it in the same manner, and the patient should endure for a few days.
Chapter Sixty-Three.
On incision of the fleshy urethra and its treatment.
Know that incision on this urethra is one of the dangerous procedures leading to destruction in most cases, therefore we see it left alone for safety. I will mention the procedures regarding it and the types of swelling.
I say that various swellings may occur in the body parts that constitute the genitals, and this can be due to many causes, either from sharp residue that flows into the genitals or from a blow. The color of the swelling is like the color of the body, and it does not discharge water.
The swelling may be soft, and sometimes the swelling is hard, its color like a plum, and it has no sensation. It could be due to the entanglement and swelling of arteries as previously mentioned, or from the swelling of veins. If it is due to the swelling of arteries, this can be identified by the dispersion of the swelling.
If you press it with your fingers, it should not be subjected to cutting at all. As for what is due to the swelling of veins, nothing disperses when pressed with fingers. This type may be incised along with other flesh.
This involves incising the scrotal skin, then elevating the testicle upwards and extracting it from the white membrane. You free the spermatic cord from the vessels, tie off the vessels, and cut the spermatic cord after freeing it from all sides of the testicle. If the testicle has adhered to the surrounding flesh.
It is necessary to extract the abscess and cut it, and if there is adhesion between some of the membranes or among the vessels, it is necessary to completely remove all that adhesion and cut it in a circular manner.
If the flesh growth is in the attachment area which is at the back, it is necessary to cut all of it and extract the abscess as we said. Once your work is done, wash the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and drink, then treat it with all treatments until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Four.
On the treatment of aden in the groin.
The aden is a twisted swelling similar to a cluster, accompanied by relaxation of the testicles, making it difficult for the patient to move, exercise, and walk. In treating this condition, the approach is similar to what has been previously mentioned.
However, it is necessary to mention the procedure as performed by our predecessors. I say that the patient should sit on a high chair, then push the testicles downward with a spoon. Then hold the skin of the testicle and the vessels near the penis with your fingers.
And another servant holds them and stretches them tightly. Then, cut with a wide, sharp scalpel along the vessels until they are exposed. Then peel from each side as I mentioned in the case of the arteries in the limbs. Then, sew them with a needle containing a doubled thread.
Tie it at the first places where the aden appeared and also tie it at the end. Then, make a vertical incision in the middle along the length of the body and remove all the corrupt humidities that have gathered there.
Then treat the wound as you would other wounds that require a period for the vessels nourishing one of the ovaries to fall off, which is acceptable. If all the vessels are exposed in the ovary, it is necessary to remove one of the ovaries along with the vessels so that the egg does not lack nutrition. Before cutting the vessels, they wither and become unusable.
Chapter Fifty-Five.
On the Treatment of Urinary Incontinence.
This incontinence occurs due to a rupture that appears in the abdominal membrane extending towards the area near the groin from the abdominal openings, causing urine to leak through the hernia into one of the ovaries.
This hernia can either be due to a tear in the abdominal membrane or its extension. These two types occur due to various causes, such as a blow, a jump, a shout, lifting something heavy, and so on. Its sign, if it is due to the extension of the abdominal membrane, is that it occurs gradually over a long period of time.
It does not happen suddenly, and the swelling is smooth to a certain depth because the abdominal membrane compresses the urine. Its sign, if it is due to a tear in the abdominal membrane, is that it causes severe pain immediately from the beginning, and the swelling appears differently under the skin, close by.
This occurs when urine exits and moves outside the abdominal membrane, and sometimes mucus may come out with the urine. This incontinence is called urinary and mucous, and it can also occur with gas. Sometimes feces may mix with the urine and get stuck there, leading to the patient's demise.
For it causes severe pain and gurgling, especially if squeezed. The treatment of these types of ailments with iron is dangerous so you should be wary of it. The method is to order the patient to return the excrement by hand into his body if returning is possible.
Then he lies on his back before you and raises his legs. Then stretch the skin next to the scrotum upwards and cut the skin of the testicles entirely lengthwise, then sew the edges of the incision with needles according to what is needed to open the incision with them.
The incision should be large enough for the egg to come out. Then peel off the membranes under the skin of the testicle until the hard white membrane is exposed on all sides. At that point, insert your index finger next to the egg.
Between the white membrane under the egg's skin and the second membrane, separate the adhesion behind the egg. Then fold it with your right hand inside the scrotal skin. At the same time, stretch the white membrane upwards with your left hand and lift the egg with the membrane to the side of the incision.
You order the servant to lift the egg upwards, and you completely separate the adhesion behind it. Check with your finger to ensure there is no twisted intestine in the hard white membrane. If you find any, push it down into the abdomen below.
Then take a needle with a thick thread that is made of ten strands and insert it at the end of the membrane under the scrotal skin near the incision. Then cut the ends of the thread twists until there are four threads. Then they are arranged one upon the other in a stiff form and are tightly tied to the peritoneum, which we mentioned is under the skin of the scrotum, from both sides. Then the ends of the threads are also wrapped up and tightly tied so that nothing of the vessels that nourish them can reach them. So that a hot swelling does not occur, and also becomes a second external binding coming out from the first binding at a distance of less than two fingers. After these two bindings, leave from the peritoneum which is under the skin of the scrotum to the length of a finger bone.
So that a hot swelling does not occur, and also becomes a second external binding coming out from the first binding at a distance of less than two fingers. After these two bindings, leave from the peritoneum which is under the skin of the scrotum to the length of a finger bone. And all the rest is cut around, and the testicle is removed with it. Then a slit is made at the bottom of the scrotal skin from which blood flows as we described earlier, then use wool soaked in oil and place it in the wound, and apply the binding as described.
And the white peritoneum, which we mentioned after cutting it, may be cauterized to prevent blood from flowing, as this often happens. The binding is left until it falls off by itself; if its falling off is delayed, then wash it with hot water and apply something that makes it sweat until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with the usual treatments for wounds until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Six.
On Hydrocele This wind-induced hydrocele, I have not seen anyone dare to treat it with surgery. The ancients mentioned that it should be done as we described for the hydrocele with a fold, which is to tie the vessels gently after making an incision below.
Then it is cut in the middle and the tumor is treated with what opens it until the vessels fall off, and the wound is treated as we have mentioned until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Seven.
On the hernia that occurs in the groin.
A hernia may appear in the groin as we have said, where the area protrudes but nothing of the intestine descends to the thighs; if it does descend, it is only slightly and returns at all times.
However, if the condition persists over time, the split in the abdominal wall increases until the intestine and the hernia descend into the scrotum. This occurs due to the extension of the abdominal wall that is in the groin, as we have said. This is because the abdominal wall extends, then relaxes and weakens the area, causing it to protrude. Its treatment is by cauterization, as I have described previously.
It can also be treated with iron in this manner: the patient lies on their back in front of you, then you make a transverse incision at the site of the swollen hernia, about three fingers wide, and then you cauterize the abdominal walls that are under the skin.
Until the white abdominal layer beneath is exposed, then take a probe and place it on the protruding part of the abdominal wall, pressing it to the depth of the abdomen. Then sew the two protruding areas at the end of the probe on the abdominal wall together with stitches.
Then withdraw the probe without cutting the abdominal wall at all, and do not touch the testicle or anything else, as I informed you in the treatment of intestinal hernia. Then treat it as you would treat wounds.
When the threads are cut, clean them and set the wound until it heals, for the hernia retracts and does not increase the swelling.
And cauterization is better in this place because it is closer to safety.
Chapter Sixty-Eight.
On the Relaxation of the Scrotal Skin.
The skin of the scrotum often relaxes in some people without the inner flesh relaxing, which makes it unappealing to look at. It is appropriate for one who wishes to treat it to have the patient lie on their back.
Cut all the relaxed skin on the thick skin, then bring the edges together. If you want, first sew the excess relaxed skin with three or four sutures and ensure the sutures are secure, then cut what is between the sutures.
Then treat it as you would other wounds until it heals and the stitches fall off.
Chapter Sixty-Nine.
On Castration.
Castration is forbidden in our religion.
For this reason, it would have been better for me not to mention it in this book. However, I mentioned it for two reasons: the first is so that it may be known to the doctor if questioned about it and to know how to treat those who undergo it. The second reason is that we often need to castrate some animals for our benefit.
Like rams and bulls and cats and the like of animals, I say that castration is of two types: either by compression or by incision and cutting. That which is done by compression, its method is to situate the animal in hot water until its testicles relax, soften, and dangle.
Then compress them with your hand until they dissolve and are no longer discernible upon touch. As for castration by incision and cutting, you should hold the animal, grasp the skin of its testicles with your left hand, then tie the scrotum and make one cut on each testicle.
Until the two testicles protrude, then cut them after you peel them and do not leave any of the membranes except for the thin membrane that covers the vessels. This method of castration is better than the one done by compression.
Because compression may leave some of the testicles, causing the animal to still desire mating. Then treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Seventy.
On the treatment of intersex conditions.
Intersex conditions in men occur in two types. The first is when there appears below the pubic area or in the skin of the scrotum between the testicles a form resembling a female vagina, with hair, and urine may flow from that which is in the scrotal skin.
As for women, there is one type, and it appears above the vagina on the pubic hair area, small and protruding outward, one resembling a man's penis and the other two like testicles. The treatment for the three types.
The two types of men and the one type of women should have that excess flesh cut until its trace is removed, then treat it like other wounds until it heals. As for the second type of men from whom urine comes out in the scrotal skin, there is no treatment for it nor any cure at all.
Chapter Seventy-One.
On the excision of the clitoris and the flesh protruding from women's genitals.
The clitoris may sometimes exceed the natural size, becoming ugly and displeasing to look at. It may also enlarge in some women until it spreads like that of men and becomes conducive to intercourse.
It should be grasped with your hand or a forceps and cut, but do not overcut, especially at the depth of the base, to avoid bleeding.
Then treat it like other wounds until it heals. As for the protruding flesh, it grows in the mouth of the womb until it fills it.
And it may sometimes protrude outward like a tail. For this reason, some early practitioners called it the tail disease. It should be cut like the clitoris and treated until it heals.
Chapter Seventy-Two.
On the Treatment of Hernia.
Hernia is when the woman's vagina is not perforated or the opening is very small, which can either be natural from birth or acquired. The acquired type results from a previous condition and may be due to excessive protruding flesh.
Or it is thin or thick adhesion, and it may be in the depth of the uterus or on its sides or at its top or bottom, and it prevents sexual intercourse and conception and childbirth, and sometimes it prevents menstruation, and knowledge of this is by the observation of the midwife.
If the obstruction is apparent and close, then if it is not apparent, examine it with her fingers or with an instrument. If the obstruction is from thin adhesion and is close to the lips, then immediately puncture it, which means make something like a guide on the lips, then place your thumbs of both hands together.
And the woman lies on her back with her legs spread apart, then she stretches the lips forcefully until she punctures the thin adhesion and the obstruction opens. Then she takes wool, soaks it in oil, and places it on the area, and has intercourse with the woman every day so that the area does not close again.
If the adhesion is thick and dense, it should be cut with a broad lancet resembling a reed leaf. If the obstruction is from grown flesh, then attach it with forceps and cut it. Have medicines that stop bleeding without stinging, such as squills, saffron, and frankincense mixed with egg white.
Then use a wide lead tube to prevent the wound from closing quickly, keep it in place for several days, and use a wick of dry linen. Then treat it with all treatments for healing until it is healed. Sometimes other flesh growths may appear in the uterus, which should be cut according to this method.
Unless it is a cancerous tumor, for a cancerous tumor in the uterus should not be treated with iron at all.
Chapter Seventy-Three.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, warts, and red blisters that appear in women's genitals.
As for hemorrhoids, it is the swelling of vein ends until much continuous blood flows from them. When hemorrhoids develop further, they become warts. I have mentioned in the classification their types and signs, and I will mention here.
What can be treated and what cannot be treated, so I say that if the hemorrhoids and warts are deep inside the uterus and not visible to the senses, they cannot be treated with iron. What is located at the mouth of the uterus and can be felt is what can be treated.
It is advisable that the woman enter a cool room, then stretch the warts with a scoop or a rough cloth, cut them from their roots, and then apply one of the blood-stopping powders without lubrication when bleeding occurs.
Such as scammony, sylphion, mastic, and the like. Then she should raise her legs against the wall for an hour, then dangle them in cold water. If the bleeding persists, sit her in a broth of sorrel, pomegranate peel, elecampane, and the like. Then take barley flour and knead it with honey and vinegar.
And apply it to her back; if the bleeding stops, otherwise persist with leeches on the spine and breasts without restriction. Then take a piece of wool, soak it in the juice of euphorbia or the juice of bistort or the juice of white thorn branches mixed with elecampane drink, and keep it in place.
When the swelling subsides, treat the area with ointment until it heals. As for the red boil, it resembles the heads of hemorrhoids, rough in appearance; you should cut off what appears of it as mentioned regarding warts, and treat it until it heals.
Chapter Seventy-Four.
On the abscess that occurs in the uterus.
Various types of tumors may occur in the uterus, such as cancer, calcified tumor, ulcers, leukorrhea, corrosive lesions, polyps, hemorrhoids, fissures, warts, and hot tumors. I have mentioned all these diseases, their types, and their symptoms in the classification.
It is necessary to mention in this article the hot tumor that occurs in the uterus, if it is one of the tumors that gather over a period, how it should be treated with iron. You should observe if the pain of the tumor at its onset is sharp, accompanied by pulsation, inflammation, and fever.
And if you see that it is red and sensitive to touch, do not rush to treat it with cautery. Instead, treat it in a way that aids its maturation. Once these symptoms subside, then the woman should sit on a chair with two seats and lean on her back.
She should bring her legs together toward the lower abdomen, with her thighs spread apart, and place her arms under her knees, securing them with a suitable binding.
For this purpose, the midwife should sit on the right side and use the instrument that opens the uterus, whose image will be shown later. If you wish to use this instrument, you must estimate with a probe the depth of the woman's uterus so that the part of the instrument inserted does not exceed the depth of the uterus.
The patient is harmed if the instrument exceeds the depth, so pads should be placed on the edge of the cervix to prevent the entire instrument from entering the depth of the womb, and the spiral that runs in the upper part of the instrument should become.
You hold the instrument and the servant turns the spiral until the cervix opens, then if the pus appears and is felt by hand and is soft and thin, it should be cut at its head with a broad scalpel, then when all the pus is drained.
A soft wick should be placed in the wound, soaked in rose oil or green oil that has some astringent properties. The wick should extend out from the incision in the cervix, and outside on the womb and the pubic area, clean wool soaked in water boiled with alum should be applied.
Then it is treated after two days with the ointment suitable for that until it heals.
The womb and the wound may be washed by injecting them with water and honey, then with water in which buckthorn root or long colocynth has been boiled, then return to the ointment, if the pus is hidden inside the womb.
It should be treated without using iron but rather with what we mentioned in the division.
Chapter Seventy-Five.
On instructing midwives how to treat live fetuses that emerge in an unnatural position.
The midwife should first know the form of natural childbirth. Among its signs are when you see the woman straining downwards and desiring to breathe in air, and her labor becomes easier for her.
And the fetus is quickly delivered, so know that this birth takes place in a natural form and it comes out head first with the afterbirth with it or hanging from its navel. When you see these signs, you should compress her abdomen so that the fetus may be delivered quickly.
For if it descends head first, the afterbirth comes with it and is cleansed well of those superfluous matters. Any birth other than this is unnatural and blameworthy because the fetus may come out feet first or hands before the head and feet.
It may come out with one hand or one leg, or its head and a hand, or folded up, and it might turn upside down, and other blameworthy forms. The midwife should be skilled and delicate in all these matters and beware of errors and mistakes.
And I clarify each of these forms and how to handle them so that you may understand and be prepared. If the fetus comes out head first in a natural manner, but the woman finds it difficult and labor becomes hard for her, and you see her strength weakening, then sit her on a chair and have women hold her steady.
Bind her womb with cooked fenugreek and moist ointments, then the midwife should insert a small forceps between her fingers to tear the afterbirth or tear it with her fingernail until the moisture inside flows out, and compress the woman's abdomen until the fetus is delivered.
If it does not come out, the woman should be injected with fenugreek juice mixed with suet. After the injection, she should be ordered to bear down and sneeze with cantharides, and her mouth and nose should be held, for then the fetus will be delivered. If the hands of the fetus come out first, they should be gently pushed back little by little.
If they cannot enter, place the woman on a stool and raise her legs up. Then shake the stool on the ground while the woman holds on so she does not fall when shaken. If both hands do not enter and the fetus dies, cut them off and pull out the rest of the fetus.
Or tie his hands with a cloth and pull them gently, for it will come out. The delivery of the fetus feet first: if the fetus comes out feet first, you should push them upwards then gradually turn the fetus until it is aligned, then take one of its legs and stretch it little by little.
When they reach the thighs, order her to squat and tickle her with a feather, for it will come out. If it does not come out as described, then gradually return the fetus until it is in its natural position, for it will then come out smoothly. If it resists all of the above methods.
Take the saliva of linseed and fenugreek, fat of sheep's tail, and dissolved gum, and mix all thoroughly in a mortar. Then apply it to the woman's vagina and lower abdomen. Then sit her in lukewarm water until it reaches the hips.
When you see that the lower part has softened, make a suppository of honey and have her hold it. Once she holds the suppository for an hour, sit her on a chair, then tickle her and close her mouth and nose, gently press her lower abdomen, and the fetus will come out at once. The delivery of the fetus knees and hands first.
If it comes out in this manner, slowly insert your hands little by little. Then the woman should lie on her back with her legs hanging down while lying on a bed, hold her hands together, and gently press above her abdomen little by little. Then remove the pillows under her legs until the lower part is raised. If the fetus does not come out, take both of her legs and move them violently. Then squeeze above the pubic bones little by little until the fetus rises up. Then the midwife inserts her hand and adjusts the fetus little by little.
Order the woman to strain so that the fetus comes out. If the fetus comes out with one of its hands extended, try to retract the hand. If she cannot retract it, make her stand and walk. If she cannot walk, have her lie down.
Place her on her bed and shake her legs violently. Then use the levers I described from the labor aids. If she is seized by labor, sit her on a chair, then work on retracting the hand and adjusting the fetus to its natural position. Make the woman sneeze and order her to strain until it comes out.
If the fetus comes out on its back with its arms extended and its face toward its mother's back, the midwife should grasp the fetus's hand, then turn it little by little and adjust it gently. Once it is in position, apply what we described of oil and labor aids to its front.
Then instruct her to move little by little. Once she does that, sit her on the chair and have her lean to the right side. Then tell her to strain and make her sneeze with cinder, for it will come out, the fetus coming out upright on its side.
If it descends to the mouth of the womb with the afterbirth, cut the afterbirth with your nail until it is drained of moisture. If it is attached to the face and neck of the fetus, cut it from the navel so that it does not choke and die. Then push the fetus inside until it is in the proper position.
And order the woman to exert herself several times, for it will come out easily like twins or many fetuses. Know that twins are often born, and three or four may be born and live, though this is rare. As for five, it is something against nature and they do not live at all.
And one placenta surrounds them even if they are many, and they are separated by a membrane barrier between each of them, tied at the navel of each one. They may come out as a single fetus does, in a natural and easy birth, or they may come out in a disliked manner as we described.
If some of them are difficult to deliver and become in the abnormal forms we mentioned, treat them as described. Let the midwife be gentle and do what she does with tenderness and caution, and adapt to each form with the skill that leads to safety.
What may be conceived in the womb and then abort: In the womb, there may be one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more than ten. It has been verified to me that a woman aborted seven, and another aborted fifteen, all of them having been conceived.
By the wisdom and knowledge of the Exalted, all of this should be within the knowledge of the midwife, for such situations may fall upon her one day, and she should handle them as is appropriate.
Chapter Sixty-Seven.
On the Extraction of a Stillborn Fetus.
If you have treated the stillborn fetus with the methods mentioned in the treatment section and it has not come out, and you are compelled to use your hands, then you should examine whether the woman is strong and free from any symptoms that might cause harm. If so, the woman should lie on her back on a bed.
Her head should be tilted downward and her legs raised, with an attendant holding her on both sides or securing her to the bed so that her body does not shift when delivering the fetus.
Then, she moistens the mouth of the womb with wet ointments, mixed with the saliva of the linseed, fenugreek, and flax seeds. The midwife then applies these ointments and salves to her hands, gently inserts them into the womb, and seeks a place to insert the hooks for the fetus, finding suitable locations for that purpose.
If the fetus is in a position to descend headfirst, insert the hooks into its eyes or the back of its head or its mouth or its palate or under its chin or its cheeks or in areas close to the ribs or under the floating ribs.
And if it is descending feet first, insert the hooks into the thighs and the middle ribs. The hook should be held with the right hand, with its bend placed between the fingers of the left hand, gently inserting the hand and piercing one of those areas we mentioned.
Until you reach an empty space, then insert another hook opposite it or a third one if needed, so that the pulling is even and does not lean to one side. Then pull steadily, and do not just pull in a straight line but move it in all directions.
To facilitate its exit, as is done when extracting a tooth, it is advisable to loosen the pull if one part is stuck. The midwife should apply some ointment to her fingers and insert them from the side to rotate what is stuck. If part of the fetus comes out, move the hooks to other positions.
It is raised slightly to do this until the fetus comes out entirely. If a hand comes out first and cannot be returned due to compression, it should be wrapped with a cloth, then pulled until it all comes out, then cut it.
Either in the wrist joint or in the elbow, and so it should be done with the other hand and the legs. If the fetus's head is large and faces compression during delivery or if there is accumulated water in its head, it should be necessary to insert a spiked forceps between the fingers.
It is used to split the head so that the water comes out or crush it with an instrument called the mashdakh, whose image comes with the images of other instruments in the section that follows this.
Similarly, if the fetus naturally has a large head, you should split or crush the skull with the mashdakh as mentioned, then extract the bones with forceps. If the head comes out and is compressed at the clavicle, it should be cut until the moisture in the chest flows out.
Then the chest will contract. If the chest does not contract and cannot come out, cut it as much as you can. If the lower abdomen is swollen or has a tumor, it should be pressed to allow the moisture to flow out.
If the fetus is in a breech position, pulling it out is easy and aligning it to the mouth of the womb is simple. If it is compressed at the abdomen or chest, you should pull it with a cloth wrapped around your hand and cut the abdomen or chest until what is inside flows out.
If all the members are extracted and the head returns and is retained, then the midwife should insert the left hand; if the mouth of the womb is open, she inserts her hand into the neck of the womb and seeks with it the head and pulls it with the fingers to the mouth of the womb, then she inserts a forceps or two forceps and pulls it with them.
If the mouth of the womb has closed due to a hot swelling, it should not be forcibly treated. Instead, at that time, moist and fatty substances should be applied, poultices used, and sitting in water that relaxes and moisturizes is recommended.
And if the fetus is on its side, if it can be aligned, then use what we mentioned for a live fetus. If that cannot be done, it should be cut and removed. It is essential not to leave any part of the afterbirth inside at all. Once you have finished your treatment, apply what we mentioned for the hot swellings that occur in the wombs.
If bleeding occurs, she should bathe in constricting waters and apply the other treatments. I have witnessed a woman who had been pregnant, and the fetus died inside her, then she became pregnant again while still carrying the deceased fetus.
Then the other fetus also died. After a long time, a swelling appeared in her uterus, and it swelled until it ruptured and began to discharge pus. I was called to treat her, and I treated her for a long time, but the wound would not heal, so I applied some of the strong drawing ointments to it.
A bone came out from the site, then after some days, another bone came out. I was amazed by this because the abdomen is a place without bones, so I estimated that they were bones from the dead fetus. I examined the wound and extracted many bones from the fetal head.
I continued doing that until I extracted many bones from her, and the woman was in the best of conditions. She lived for a time with some pus draining from the site, and I have presented this rarity here.
Because it contains knowledge and assistance for what the skilled doctor attempts to treat with his hands.
Chapter Seventy-Seven.
It contains images of the tools needed for extracting the fetus.
An image of a speculum used to open the mouth of the womb:.
This clamp, with which books are aligned, has two screws at the ends of the two pieces of wood. However, this screw should be finer than the clamp and should be made either of ebony or boxwood, and the width of each piece of wood should be the thickness of two fingers.
And their ends are rounded like a finger, and their length is about one and a half fingers. In the middle of the two pieces of wood are two protrusions made of the same type of wood, securely attached to them. Their length should be about half a finger or slightly more, and their width should be around two fingers or slightly more. These protrusions
are the ones that enter into the mouth of the womb to open it when you turn the screws. An image of another tool for the same purpose, finer and lighter:.
It is made from ebony or boxwood in the shape of forceps, except that it has two protrusions at the end as you see. The length of each protrusion is about one finger, and their width is two fingers. When you want to open the womb with them,.
Sit the woman on a bed with her legs hanging down and spread apart, then insert these two rods together into the mouth of the womb while you hold the end of the instrument below between her thighs, then open your hand with the instrument as you would with forceps according to how much opening of the womb you desire.
